<UserId.>117573059899874027403</UserId.><username>Jen G< /username><Time>1484449008808<//Time><Rating>1</Rating>< Text>
Towing companies need to follow rules and laws for private property.  They are required to have signed authorization from Property Management or an authorized agent of Property Management.  This has to have correct and legit information on it.  Including contact information- phone #- employee name- title- etc.  If for any reason you are refused this- example- employee does not have access- manager is not here- its after hours- its a holiday.  File a police report under vehicle code: 22658.  The police will then know how to report the violation-  Its an unauthorized predatory tow.  And you will have a record that they refused you this fundamental right.

Towing companies are legally obligated to give you signed authorization and more before you even pay for your car.  Best thing to do is pay- get your car back- file police report- take them to small claims for 4x your  fees.

If your rights have been violated you can report to the better business bureau- to report unethical business practices.<//Text>

We drive a long way to get our excellent Yucateco food from here, every Christmas for the past few years.  The food is delicious and I wish we lived closer to come here on a more regular basis.  Annie has the most exceptional customer service, always willing to keep the customers happy.  I totally recommend the tamales colados, vaporcitos, cochinita pibil, frijoles negros colados and rice.  The hojaldra is divine.  WE LOVE THIS PLACE!</Review>

<username>Ruben Cruz</username><Gmap_id>0x80c2c793c5b671b1:0x2b4a157270528f21<//Gmap_id></record></dataset><record>

< Review>
A trip to a nearby auto upholstery shop left me wandering around Pico-Union for a few hours with a sleepy baby in a stoller.  Was very lucky to find this place.  It's a really nice, completely family run bakery.  I love their baked goods--they even recommended a guava filled pastry that didn't have any dairy for my allergic toddler.  What really shines is their Cochinita Pibil, Lomitas (only on Thurs/Fri) and their tamales.  The cochinita pibil is a pork stew that is great in sandwiches(tortas), on tacos, or do like me--I buy it by the pound and eat it for a week over rice.  They serve it with pickled onions that provides a nice sour counter punch to the stew's umami goodness. Go there more then once and they'll be greeting you by name.  I hope this place continues to do great, and someday graduates to full restaurant.</Review>

<userid>109330704821620741315</userid>< name>
Steve Tu</name>
< Time>
1468259450198</Time>
< rating>
4<//rating>
<review>FOOD
I had a serious ramen craving tonight. For twice the price and a brutally long commute, I could've gone to Daikokuya over by Downtown LA for the best ramen in LA, but tonight I was feeling something "cheap and decent." And Tokyo Fast Food did just the trick.

I had the Tonkatsu Ramen with extra Chashu (added $0.50, not bad for 2 extra slices). For the price (just a little over $7), it was quite good. The broth wasn't nearly as fatty-satisfying as Daikokuya, but I'd say it's just a hair below Asahi (over on Sawtelle) for less $. I'll take that on most nights.

My friend had the Tokyo Special. He said it was pretty decent too. Again, for the price, pretty darn good and excellent quantity.

I'm bringing my own soup spoon next time, because they only handed me a plastic spoon, haha.

ENVIRONMENT
Parking wasn't too bad, but then again we went at 7:15pm on a Thursday. I'd expect parking to be worse at a more peak time. So watch out for that. I liked the homey/hole-in-the-wall feel.

I'm going back sometime. I like :-)

<Text>THEY CHARGED FOR A WATER CUP.
My sick&dying grandfather was craving a pizza, so I took him here with my mom. It was a late and cool night, but the restaurant was extremely hot. We walked in to find the doors wide open with no customers, no fans or A/C on, and little lighting. The cashier was friendly, he was the owner's nephew and he seemed like a nice kid. We ordered a pizza that came out greasier than my brother's face after football practice. The owner brought out our pizza and peeled apart the cheapest paper plates, exactly three for our table and exactly three napkins. The pizza grease bled through the plates and I used all three napkins, having to get up for more. I was too afraid to wash my hands in the restroom because the long hallway had no lights on and the walk was too sketchy. The most disturbing part to me was the fact that we had to pay 50¬¢ per cup for water, I cannot eat at a restaurant that charges for water, especially to my sickly grandfather. While the owner was nice and the pizza was decent, the owner is too much of a cheapskate to keep this place in business for much longer. I suggest that other people take their business elsewhere.</Text>< gmap_id>

<time>1572164147482</time><Rating>5<//Rating>< text>
Bunny friendly hotel! We were at a last resort calling hotels in the area to find ANY that accepted pet owners since we had just checked out of the worst hotel experience at Motel 6 a few blocks away. To our astonishment a guy answered my call and said: well bunnies are small creatures so we‚Äôd count your two bunnies as one pet fee, $25. No exhorbitant pricing like other hotels, (some are $150 per night, plus cleaning fee, pricing us out at the start which is kind of a switch and bait for the pet friendly icon) upfront kind assistance unlike other places.
We checked in and it was extremely busy - people checking in were kinda tired and crotchety in the queue. But the staff (clearly overloaded) were completely unphased warm and welcoming. I was shocked because my prior experience around the corner at motel 6 made us feel entirely unwelcome by the managing staff of their local competitor.
One guy stood out and really took the lead in helping us out. Mr. Bruce Wayne, personally checked on some difficulties I was having with working out the TV. He explained it was an unusual night as people were checking in from surrounding brush fire. Inspite of all this commotion all the staff were highly welcoming, and made me feel like my last months hotel hopping should have gone this way!
In addition... I was completely surprised how well the rooms were fitted out with amenities for a price on par with motel 6. There was a kitchen! Perfect for pet owners, and the furniture was nice. Well appointed rooms and large refrigerator for the bunnies veggies. From now on I will always check out extended stay and recommend it to visiting relatives :)<//text>

< text>
I had the misfortune of staying at this hotel for two weeks on business.  I've stayed at four different Extended Stay Americas in LA County, and this is the worst one.

The first thing I noticed upon entering the lobby was the smell of tobacco mixed with a myriad of other unpleasant odors.  This scent permeates the entire building.  The hallways are now lined with air fresheners which serve to mask the stench.  Luckily, I travel with a small air purifier, so at least my room was all right after a day or so.

The hallways are dimly lit.  The hotel is in an L shape, and the length of the long hallway gave me some "Shining" vibes.  It's difficult to navigate a luggage trolley into and out of the hotel's single elevator, and guests frequently try to enter the elevator without checking to make sure nobody's getting out first.

On my first night, I asked for a kitchen set and was given roughly half of what the entire set included.  They told me to check back later if I still needed anything more.  The next day I wrote a list of what was missing and brought it to the front desk.  I still didn't receive everything that was missing.  I asked the man at the front desk for two spoons, and he asked me to wait while he got the two spoons he knew were available.  He went one direction, came back with a plastic spoon, then pointed another direction, saying he remembered the other being over there.  He went that way and returned with the second plastic spoon.  So, the hotel had two spoons available, they were both plastic, they were from different sets, and I had both of them.  I gave up on the rest of the kitchen set after that.

At least I didn't find anything awful with my room, which is why I give this hotel two stars.  Also, individual employees were nice and tried to be helpful, despite what they had to work with.  But I can't give more than two stars given the conditions.

During my entire stay, there were shady people loitering about in the parking lot and the side of the building.  I didn't feel particularly safe, and I thought it was odd, since the surrounding area doesn't seem to be so bad.  People frequently parked their cars across spaces in the parking lot.  On my last day here, they did start towing cars away, so it seems they're trying to crack down on that.

Just before I left, they hired a security guard to check people who were entering the hotel lobby and to discourage people from loitering.  My impression when I left was that management is making an effort to turn things around.< /text>

I called the next day and I was told there were no pillows. I had one bar of used soap in the shower. I asked if they had cleaned this room? The floor was gross. It was pretty scary to say the least, and people coming in the side door that I do not think should be there? They came in when we would open the door to leave, they would wait by the door, very shady looking characters, one guy was so messed up by the side door and very scary he was just starring in the door waiting for someone to leave 10pm at night, I had to use the front door to leave. There was a gal who looked like she was living in her car, she was real jittery and tryed talking to me I just did not answer, and a tow truck showed up hours later to tow her and she was arguing with the guy. I am not sure why you would ask for a review because I doubt you would do anything. Of course I did not expect the Hilton. I stayed at an Extended Stay America with my entire family a few years back when we had our reunion and it was nice, and the peope were very nice there too!  I know the price is fair for the area, but not for what I saw and experienced after I arrived. Had I extra money I would have stayed somewhere else and forfeited the money I paid to Priceline. This was a special trip I did for my kids and this was a terrible experience!! I am a single mother on a limited budget and I thought I was getting a decent place for the price this is why I spent alittle more then a $50 motel. I do not think I should have been charged for a cot that had no bedding with it either! It is a very scetchy place, with very scetchy people living there. I think it does not cost that much to have extra pillows, and tv's that work, and a business shirt for your employees to wear! You could even hire people once in awhile to clean up the garbage on the property. I do not mind either not having any service when I am only staying at a place for 2 days to conserve water and save money for hired help, but I do mind that a place is just somewhat clean and safe and not smelling drugs in the doors by the stairwells.
